Wayne Denning has produced multiple national advertising campaigns and even created the first ever Australian segment for internationally-beloved children’s series Sesame Street. But along with the innovation inherent in any creative industry, his biggest challenge remains educating the local market that Indigenous business can add significant value to the economic landscape.

<div class="fc-item__header">
<h2 class="fc-item__title"><a href="https://www.theguardian.com/cities/2017/aug/23/america-alt-weeklies-baltimore-city-paper-village-voice" class="fc-item__link" data-link-name="article"><span class="fc-item__kicker">America's 'news deserts'</span> <span class="u-faux-block-link__cta fc-item__headline"> <span class="js-headline-text">The death of the great alt-weeklies</span></span> </a></h2>
</div>
<div class="fc-item__standfirst">
The Village Voice’s decision to end print publication is just the latest in an epidemic of free alternative newspaper closures in the US, which have left many cities with no local journalism at all. Is there hope for alt-weeklies?
</div>
<aside class="fc-item__meta js-item__meta">
</aside>
</div>
